## 3900 **Appendix B. Mandatory normative statement (non-** 3901 **normative)** 

3902 This Appendix is non-normative and is provided as a convenient summary of the numbered conformance 3903 statements found in the main body of this document. Refer to Chapter 7 for a definitive list of 3904 conformance requirements. 

3905 

|**Normative**<br>**Statement**<br>**Number**|**Normative Statement**|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-1.5.4-1]|The character data in a UTF-8 Encoded String MUST be well-formed UTF-8 as defined<br>by the Unicode specification [Unicode] and restated in RFC 3629 [RFC3629]. In<br>particular, the character data MUST NOT include encodings of code points between<br>U+D800 and U+DFFF.|
|[MQTT-1.5.4-2]|A UTF-8 Encoded String MUST NOT include an encoding of the null character U+0000.|
|[MQTT-1.5.4-3]|A UTF-8 encoded sequence 0xEF 0xBB 0xBF is always interpreted as U+FEFF ("ZERO<br>WIDTH NO-BREAK SPACE") wherever it appears in a string and MUST NOT be skipped<br>over or stripped off by a packet receiver.|
|[MQTT-1.5.5-1]|The encoded value MUST use the minimum number of bytes necessary to represent the<br>value.|
|[MQTT-1.5.7-1]|Both strings MUST comply with the requirements for UTF-8 Encoded Strings.|
|[MQTT-2.1.3-1]|Where a flag bit is marked as “Reserved” it is reserved for future use and MUST be set to<br>the value listed.|
|[MQTT-2.2.1-2]|A PUBLISH packet MUST NOT contain a Packet Identifier if its QoS value is set to 0.|
|[MQTT-2.2.1-3]|Each time a Client sends a new SUBSCRIBE, UNSUBSCRIBE,or PUBLISH (where QoS<br>> 0) MQTT Control Packet it MUST assign it a non-zero Packet Identifier that is currently<br>unused.|
|[MQTT-2.2.1-4]|Each time a Server sends a new PUBLISH (with QoS > 0) MQTT Control Packet it MUST<br>assign it a non zero Packet Identifier that is currently unused.|
|[MQTT-2.2.1-5]|A PUBACK, PUBREC, PUBREL, or PUBCOMP packet MUST contain the same Packet<br>Identifier as the PUBLISH packet that was originally sent.|
|[MQTT-2.2.1-6]|A SUBACK and UNSUBACK MUST contain the Packet Identifier that was used in the<br>corresponding SUBSCRIBE and UNSUBSCRIBE packet respectively.|
|[MQTT-2.2.2-1]|If there are no properties, this MUST be indicated by including a Property Length of zero.|
|[MQTT-3.1.0-1]|After a Network Connection is established by a Client to a Server, the first packet sent<br>from the Client to the Server MUST be a CONNECT packet.|
|[MQTT-3.1.0-2]|The Server MUST process a second CONNECT packet sent from a Client as a Protocol<br>Error and close the Network Connection.|



07 March 2019 Page 121 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-3.1.2-1]|The protocol name MUST be the UTF-8 String "MQTT". If the Server does not want to<br>accept the CONNECT, and wishes to reveal that it is an MQTT Server it MAY send a<br>CONNACK packet with Reason Code of 0x84 (Unsupported Protocol Version), and then<br>it MUST close the Network Connection.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-2]|If the Protocol Version is not 5 and the Server does not want to accept the CONNECT<br>packet, the Server MAY send a CONNACK packet with Reason Code 0x84 (Unsupported<br>Protocol Version) and then MUST close the Network Connection|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-3]|The Server MUST validate that the reserved flag in the CONNECT packet is set to 0.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-4]|If a CONNECT packet is received with Clean Start is set to 1, the Client and Server<br>MUST discard any existing Session and start a new Session.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-5]|If a CONNECT packet is received with Clean Start set to 0 and there is a Session<br>associated with the Client Identifier, the Server MUST resume communications with the<br>Client based on state from the existing Session.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-6]|If a CONNECT packet is received with Clean Start set to 0 and there is no Session<br>associated with the Client Identifier, the Server MUST create a new Session.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-7]|If the Will Flag is set to 1 this indicates that, a Will Message MUST be stored on the<br>Server and associated with the Session.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-8]|The Will Message MUST be published after the Network Connection is subsequently<br>closed and either the Will Delay Interval has elapsed or the Session ends, unless the Will<br>Message has been deleted by the Server on receipt of a DISCONNECT packet with<br>Reason Code 0x00 (Normal disconnection) or a new Network Connection for the ClientID<br>is opened before the Will Delay Interval has elapsed.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-9]|If the Will Flag is set to 1, the Will QoS and Will Retain fields in the Connect Flags will be<br>used by the Server, and the Will Properties, Will Topic and Will Message fields MUST be<br>present in the Payload.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-10]|The Will Message MUST be removed from the stored Session State in the Server once it<br>has been published or the Server has received a DISCONNECT packet with a Reason<br>Code of 0x00 (Normal disconnection) from the Client.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-11]|If the Will Flag is set to 0, then the Will QoS MUST be set to 0 (0x00).|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-12]|If the Will Flag is set to 1, the value of Will QoS can be 0 (0x00), 1 (0x01), or 2 (0x02).|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-13]|If the Will Flag is set to 0, then Will Retain MUST be set to 0.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-14]|If the Will Flag is set to 1 and Will Retain is set to 0, the Server MUST publish the Will<br>Message as a non-retained message.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-15]|If the Will Flag is set to 1 and Will Retain is set to 1, the Server MUST publish the Will<br>Message as a retained message.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-16]|If the User Name Flag is set to 0, a User Name MUST NOT be present in the Payload.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-17]|If the User Name Flag is set to 1, a User Name MUST be present in the Payload.|



07 March 2019 Page 122 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-3.1.2-18]|If the Password Flag is set to 0, a Password MUST NOT be present in the Payload.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-19]|If the Password Flag is set to 1, a Password MUST be present in the Payload.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-20]|If Keep Alive is non-zero and in the absence of sending any other MQTT Control<br>Packets, the Client MUST send a PINGREQ packet.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-21]|If the Server returns a Server Keep Alive on the CONNACK packet, the Client MUST use<br>that value instead of the value it sent as the Keep Alive.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-22]|If the Keep Alive value is non-zero and the Server does not receive an MQTT Control<br>Packet from the Client within one and a half times the Keep Alive time period, it MUST<br>close the Network Connection to the Client as if the network had failed.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-23]|The Client and Server MUST store the Session State after the Network Connection is<br>closed if the Session Expiry Interval is greater than 0.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-24]|The Server MUST NOT send packets exceeding Maximum Packet Size to the Client.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-25]|Where a Packet is too large to send, the Server MUST discard it without sending it and<br>then behave as if it had completed sending that Application Message.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-26]|The Server MUST NOT send a Topic Alias in a PUBLISH packet to the Client greater<br>than Topic Alias Maximum.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-27]|If Topic Alias Maximum is absent or zero, the Server MUST NOT send any Topic Aliases<br>to the.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-28]|A value of 0 indicates that the Server MUST NOT return Response Information.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-29]|If the value of Request Problem Information is 0, the Server MAY return a Reason String<br>or User Properties on a CONNACK or DISCONNECT packet, but MUST NOT send a<br>Reason String or User Properties on any packet other than PUBLISH, CONNACK, or<br>DISCONNECT.|
|[MQTT-3.1.2-30]|If a Client sets an Authentication Method in the CONNECT, the Client MUST NOT send<br>any packets other than AUTH or DISCONNECT packets until it has received a<br>CONNACK packet.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-1]|The Payload of the CONNECT packet contains one or more length-prefixed fields, whose<br>presence is determined by the flags in the Variable Header. These fields, if present,<br>MUST appear in the order Client Identifier, Will Topic, Will Message, User Name,<br>Password.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-2]|The ClientID MUST be used by Clients and by Servers to identify state that they hold<br>relating to this MQTT Session between the Client and the Server.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-3]|The ClientID MUST be present and is the first field in the CONNECT packet Payload.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-4]|The ClientID MUST be a UTF-8 Encoded String.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-5]|The Server MUST allow ClientID’s which are between 1 and 23 UTF-8 encoded bytes in<br>length, and that contain only the characters<br>"0123456789abcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyzABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZ".|



07 March 2019 Page 123 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-3.1.3-6]|A Server MAY allow a Client to supply a ClientID that has a length of zero bytes, however<br>if it does so the Server MUST treat this as a special case and assign a unique ClientID to<br>that Client.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-7]|It MUST then process the CONNECT packet as if the Client had provided that unique<br>ClientID, and MUST return the Assigned Client Identifier in the CONNACK packet.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-8]|If the Server rejects the ClientID it MAY respond to the CONNECT packet with a<br>CONNACK using Reason Code 0x85 (Client Identifier not valid) as described in section<br>4.13 Handling errors, and then it MUST close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-9]|If a new Network Connection to this Session is made before the Will Delay Interval has<br>passed, the Server MUST NOT send the Will Message.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-10]|The Server MUST maintain the order of User Properties when forwarding the Application<br>Message.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-11]|The Will Topic MUST be a UTF-8 Encoded String.|
|[MQTT-3.1.3-12]|If the User Name Flag is set to 1, the User Name is the next field in the Payload. The<br>User Name MUST be a UTF-8 Encoded String.|
|[MQTT-3.1.4-1]|The Server MUST validate that the CONNECT packet matches the format described in<br>section 3.1 and close the Network Connection if it does not match.|
|[MQTT-3.1.4-2]|The Server MAY check that the contents of the CONNECT packet meet any further<br>restrictions and SHOULD perform authentication and authorization checks. If any of<br>these checks fail, it MUST close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.1.4-3]|If the ClientID represents a Client already connected to the Server, the Server sends a<br>DISCONNECT packet to the existing Client with Reason Code of 0x8E (Session taken<br>over) as described in section 4.13 and MUST close the Network Connection of the<br>existing Client.|
|[MQTT-3.1.4-4]|The Server MUST perform the processing of Clean Start.|
|[MQTT-3.1.4-5]|The Server MUST acknowledge the CONNECT packet with a CONNACK packet<br>containing a 0x00 (Success) Reason Code.|
|[MQTT-3.1.4-6]|If the Server rejects the CONNECT, it MUST NOT process any data sent by the Client<br>after the CONNECT packet except AUTH packets.|
|[MQTT-3.2.0-1]|The Server MUST send a CONNACK with a 0x00 (Success) Reason Code before<br>sending any Packet other than AUTH.|
|[MQTT-3.2.0-2]|The Server MUST NOT send more than one CONNACK in a Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-1]|Byte 1 is the "Connect Acknowledge Flags". Bits 7-1 are reserved and MUST be set to 0.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-2]|If the Server accepts a connection with Clean Start set to 1, the Server MUST set<br>Session Present to 0 in the CONNACK packet in addition to setting a 0x00 (Success)<br>Reason Code in the CONNACK packet.|



07 March 2019 Page 124 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-3.2.2-3]|If the Server accepts a connection with Clean Start set to 0 and the Server has Session<br>State for the ClientID, it MUST set Session Present to 1 in the CONNACK packet,<br>otherwise it MUST set Session Present to 0 in the CONNACK packet. In both cases it<br>MUST set a 0x00 (Success) Reason Code in the CONNACK packet.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-4]|If the Client does not have Session State and receives Session Present set to 1 it MUST<br>close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-5]|If the Client does have Session State and receives Session Present set to 0 it MUST<br>discard its Session State if it continues with the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-6]|If a Server sends a CONNACK packet containing a non-zero Reason Code it MUST set<br>Session Present to 0.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-7]|If a Server sends a CONNACK packet containing a Reason code of 0x80 or greater it<br>MUST then close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-8]|The Server sending the CONNACK packet MUST use one of the Connect Reason Code<br>values.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-9]|If a Server does not support QoS 1 or QoS 2 PUBLISH packets it MUST send a<br>Maximum QoS in the CONNACK packet specifying the highest QoS it supports.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-10]|A Server that does not support QoS 1 or QoS 2 PUBLISH packets MUST still accept<br>SUBSCRIBE packets containing a Requested QoS of 0, 1 or 2.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-11]|If a Client receives a Maximum QoS from a Server, it MUST NOT send PUBLISH packets<br>at a QoS level exceeding the Maximum QoS level specified.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-12]|If a Server receives a CONNECT packet containing a Will QoS that exceeds its<br>capabilities, it MUST reject the connection. It SHOULD use a CONNACK packet with<br>Reason Code 0x9B (QoS not supported) as described in section 4.13 Handling errors,<br>and MUST close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-13]|If a Server receives a CONNECT packet containing a Will Message with the Will Retain<br>1, and it does not support retained messages, the Server MUST reject the connection<br>request. It SHOULD send CONNACK with Reason Code 0x9A (Retain not supported)<br>and then it MUST close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-14]|A Client receiving Retain Available set to 0 from the Server MUST NOT send a PUBLISH<br>packet with the RETAIN flag set to 1.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-15]|The Client MUST NOT send packets exceeding Maximum Packet Size to the Server.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-16]|If the Client connects using a zero length Client Identifier, the Server MUST respond with<br>a CONNACK containing an Assigned Client Identifier. The Assigned Client Identifier<br>MUST be a new Client Identifier not used by any other Session currently in the Server.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-17]|The Client MUST NOT send a Topic Alias in a PUBLISH packet to the Server greater<br>than this value.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-18]|Topic Alias Maximum is absent, the Client MUST NOT send any Topic Aliases on to the<br>Server.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-19]|The Server MUST NOT send this property if it would increase the size of the CONNACK<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the Client.|



07 March 2019 Page 125 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-3.2.2-20]|The Server MUST NOT send this property if it would increase the size of the CONNACK<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the Client.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-21]|If the Server sends a Server Keep Alive on the CONNACK packet, the Client MUST use<br>this value instead of the Keep Alive value the Client sent on CONNECT.|
|[MQTT-3.2.2-22]|If the Server does not send the Server Keep Alive, the Server MUST use the Keep Alive<br>value set by the Client on CONNECT.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-1]|The DUP flag MUST be set to 1 by the Client or Server when it attempts to re-deliver a<br>PUBLISH packet.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-2]|The DUP flag MUST be set to 0 for all QoS 0 messages.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-3]|The DUP flag in the outgoing PUBLISH packet is set independently to the incoming<br>PUBLISH packet, its value MUST be determined solely by whether the outgoing<br>PUBLISH packet is a retransmission.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-4]|A PUBLISH Packet MUST NOT have both QoS bits set to 1.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-5]|If the RETAIN flag is set to 1 in a PUBLISH packet sent by a Client to a Server, the<br>Server MUST replace any existing retained message for this topic and store the<br>Application Message.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-6]|If the Payload contains zero bytes it is processed normally by the Server but any retained<br>message with the same topic name MUST be removed and any future subscribers for the<br>topic will not receive a retained message.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-7]|A retained message with a Payload containing zero bytes MUST NOT be stored as a<br>retained message on the Server.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-8]|If the RETAIN flag is 0 in a PUBLISH packet sent by a Client to a Server, the Server<br>MUST NOT store the message as a retained message and MUST NOT remove or<br>replace any existing retained message.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-9]|If Retain Handling is set to 0 the Server MUST send the retained messages matching the<br>Topic Filter of the subscription to the Client.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-10]|If Retain Handling is set to 1 then if the subscription did already exist, the Server MUST<br>send all retained message matching the Topic Filter of the subscription to the Client, and<br>if the subscription did not exist, the Server MUST NOT send the retained messages.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-11]|If Retain Handling is set to 2, the Server MUST NOT send the retained|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-12]|If the value of Retain As Published subscription option is set to 0, the Server MUST set<br>the RETAIN flag to 0 when forwarding an Application Message regardless of how the<br>RETAIN flag was set in the received PUBLISH packet.|
|[MQTT-3.3.1-13]|If the value of Retain As Published subscription option is set to 1, the Server MUST set<br>the RETAIN flag equal to the RETAIN flag in the received PUBLISH packet.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-1]|The Topic Name MUST be present as the first field in the PUBLISH packet Variable<br>Header. It MUST be a UTF-8 Encoded String.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-2]|The Topic Name in the PUBLISH packet MUST NOT contain wildcard characters.|



07 March 2019 Page 126 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-3.3.2-3]|The Topic Name in a PUBLISH packet sent by a Server to a subscribing Client MUST<br>match the Subscription’s Topic Filter.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-4]|A Server MUST send the Payload Format Indicator unaltered to all subscribers receiving<br>the message.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-5]|If the Message Expiry Interval has passed and the Server has not managed to start<br>onward delivery to a matching subscriber, then it MUST delete the copy of the message<br>for that subscriber.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-6]|The PUBLISH packet sent to a Client by the Server MUST contain a Message Expiry<br>Interval set to the received value minus the time that the message has been waiting in<br>the Server.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-7]|A receiver MUST NOT carry forward any Topic Alias mappings from one Network<br>Connection to another.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-8]|A sender MUST NOT send a PUBLISH packet containing a Topic Alias which has the<br>value 0.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-9]|A Client MUST NOT send a PUBLISH packet with a Topic Alias greater than the Topic<br>Alias Maximum value returned by the Server in the CONNACK packet.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-10]|A Client MUST accept all Topic Alias values greater than 0 and less than or equal to the<br>Topic Alias Maximum value that it sent in the CONNECT packet.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-11]|A Server MUST NOT send a PUBLISH packet with a Topic Alias greater than the Topic<br>Alias Maximum value sent by the Client in the CONNECT packet.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-12]|A Server MUST accept all Topic Alias values greater than 0 and less than or equal to the<br>Topic Alias Maximum value that it returned in the CONNACK packet.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-13]|The Response Topic MUST be a UTF-8 Encoded String.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-14]|The Response Topic MUST NOT contain wildcard characters.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-15]|The Server MUST send the Response Topic unaltered to all subscribers receiving the<br>Application Message.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-16]|The Server MUST send the Correlation Data unaltered to all subscribers receiving the<br>Application Message.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-17]|The Server MUST send all User Properties unaltered in a PUBLISH packet when<br>forwarding the Application Message to a Client.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-18]|The Server MUST maintain the order of User Properties when forwarding the Application<br>Message.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-19]|The Content Type MUST be a UTF-8 Encoded String.|
|[MQTT-3.3.2-20]|A Server MUST send the Content Type unaltered to all subscribers receiving the<br>Application Message.|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-1]|The receiver of a PUBLISH Packet MUST respond with the packet as determined by the<br>QoS in the PUBLISH Packet.|



07 March 2019 Page 127 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-3.3.4-2]|In this case the Server MUST deliver the message to the Client respecting the maximum<br>QoS of all the matching subscriptions.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-3]|If the Client specified a Subscription Identifier for any of the overlapping subscriptions the<br>Server MUST send those Subscription Identifiers in the message which is published as<br>the result of the subscriptions.|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-4]|If the Server sends a single copy of the message it MUST include in the PUBLISH packet<br>the Subscription Identifiers for all matching subscriptions which have a Subscription<br>Identifiers, their order is not significant.|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-5]|If the Server sends multiple PUBLISH packets it MUST send, in each of them, the<br>Subscription Identifier of the matching subscription if it has a Subscription Identifier.|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-6]|A PUBLISH packet sent from a Client to a Server MUST NOT contain a Subscription<br>Identifier.|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-7]|The Client MUST NOT send more than Receive Maximum QoS 1 and QoS 2 PUBLISH<br>packets for which it has not received PUBACK, PUBCOMP, or PUBREC with a Reason<br>Code of 128 or greater from the Server.|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-8]|The Client MUST NOT delay the sending of any packets other than PUBLISH packets<br>due to having sent Receive Maximum PUBLISH packets without receiving<br>acknowledgements for them.|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-9]|The Server MUST NOT send more than Receive Maximum QoS 1 and QoS 2 PUBLISH<br>packets for which it has not received PUBACK, PUBCOMP, or PUBREC with a Reason<br>Code of 128 or greater from the Client.|
|[MQTT-3.3.4-10]|The Server MUST NOT delay the sending of any packets other than PUBLISH packets<br>due to having sent Receive Maximum PUBLISH packets without receiving<br>acknowledgements for them.|
|[MQTT-3.4.2-1]|The Client or Server sending the PUBACK packet MUST use one of the PUBACK<br>Reason Codes.|
|[MQTT-3.4.2-2]|The sender MUST NOT send this property if it would increase the size of the PUBACK<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the receiver.|
|[MQTT-3.4.2-3]|The sender MUST NOT send this property if it would increase the size of the PUBACK<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the receiver.|
|[MQTT-3.5.2-1]|The Client or Server sending the PUBREC packet MUST use one of the PUBREC<br>Reason Codes.|
|[MQTT-3.5.2-2]|The sender MUST NOT send this property if it would increase the size of the PUBREC<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the receiver.|
|[MQTT-3.5.2-3]|The sender MUST NOT send this property if it would increase the size of the PUBREC<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the receiver.|
|[MQTT-3.6.1-1]|Bits 3,2,1 and 0 of the Fixed Header in the PUBREL packet are reserved and MUST be<br>set to 0,0,1 and 0 respectively. The Server MUST treat any other value as malformed and<br>close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-3.6.2-1]|The Client or Server sending the PUBREL packet MUST use one of the PUBREL<br>Reason Codes.|

|[MQTT-3.6.2-2]|The sender MUST NOT send this Property if it would increase the size of the PUBREL<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the receiver.|

|[MQTT-3.6.2-3]|The sender MUST NOT send this property if it would increase the size of the PUBREL<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the receiver.|

|[MQTT-3.7.2-3]|The sender MUST NOT send this property if it would increase the size of the PUBCOMP<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by receiver.|
|[MQTT-3.8.1-1]|Bits 3,2,1 and 0 of the Fixed Header of the SUBSCRIBE packet are reserved and MUST<br>be set to 0,0,1 and 0 respectively. The Server MUST treat any other value as malformed<br>and close the Network Connection|
|[MQTT-3.8.3-1]|The Topic Filters MUST be a UTF-8 Encoded String.|
|[MQTT-3.8.3-2]|The Payload MUST contain at least one Topic Filter and Subscription Options pair.|
|[MQTT-3.8.3-3]|Bit 2 of the Subscription Options represents the No Local option. If the value is 1,<br>Application Messages MUST NOT be forwarded to a connection with a ClientID equal to<br>the ClientID of the publishing connection.|
|[MQTT-3.8.3-4]|It is a Protocol Error to set the No Local bit to 1 on a Shared Subscription.|
|[MQTT-3.8.3-5]|The Server MUST treat a SUBSCRIBE packet as malformed if any of Reserved bits in<br>the Payload are non-zero.|
|[MQTT-3.8.4-1]|When the Server receives a SUBSCRIBE packet from a Client, the Server MUST<br>respond with a SUBACK packet.|
|[MQTT-3.8.4-2]|The SUBACK packet MUST have the same Packet Identifier as the SUBSCRIBE packet<br>that it is acknowledging.|
|[MQTT-3.8.4-3]|If a Server receives a SUBSCRIBE packet containing a Topic Filter that is identical to a<br>Non-shared Subscription’s Topic Filter for the current Session then it MUST replace that<br>existing Subscription with a new Subscription.|
|[MQTT-3.8.4-4]|If the Retain Handling option is 0, any existing retained messages matching the Topic<br>Filter MUST be re-sent, but Application Messages MUST NOT be lost due to replacing<br>the Subscription.|
|[MQTT-3.8.4-5]|If a Server receives a SUBSCRIBE packet that contains multiple Topic Filters it MUST<br>handle that packet as if it had received a sequence of multiple SUBSCRIBE packets,<br>except that it combines their responses into a single SUBACK response.|
|[MQTT-3.8.4-6]|The SUBACK packet sent by the Server to the Client MUST contain a Reason Code for<br>each Topic Filter/Subscription Option pair.|
|[MQTT-3.8.4-7]|This Reason Code MUST either show the maximum QoS that was granted for that<br>Subscription or indicate that the subscription failed.|

|[MQTT-3.8.4-8]|The QoS of Payload Messages sent in response to a Subscription MUST be the<br>minimum of the QoS of the originally published message and the Maximum QoS granted<br>by the Server.|

|[MQTT-3.9.2-1]|The Server MUST NOT send this Property if it would increase the size of the SUBACK<br>packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the Client.|

|[MQTT-3.10.1-1]|Bits 3,2,1 and 0 of the Fixed Header of the UNSUBSCRIBE packet are reserved and<br>MUST be set to 0,0,1 and 0 respectively. The Server MUST treat any other value as<br>malformed and close the Network Connection|
|[MQTT-3.10.3-1]|The Topic Filters in an UNSUBSCRIBE packet MUST be UTF-8 Encoded Strings.|
|[MQTT-3.10.3-2]|The Payload of an UNSUBSCRIBE packet MUST contain at least one Topic Filter.|
|[MQTT-3.10.4-1]|The Topic Filters (whether they contain wildcards or not) supplied in an UNSUBSCRIBE<br>packet MUST be compared character-by-character with the current set of Topic Filters<br>held by the Server for the Client. If any filter matches exactly then its owning Subscription<br>MUST be deleted.|
|[MQTT-3.10.4-2]|When a Server receives UNSUBSCRIBE It MUST stop adding any new messages which<br>match the Topic Filters, for delivery to the Client.|
|[MQTT-3.10.4-3]|When a Server receives UNSUBSCRIBE It MUST complete the delivery of any QoS 1 or<br>QoS 2 messages which match the Topic Filters and it has started to send to the Client.|
|[MQTT-3.10.4-4]|The Server MUST respond to an UNSUBSCRIBE request by sending an UNSUBACK<br>packet.|
|[MQTT-3.10.4-5]|The UNSUBACK packet MUST have the same Packet Identifier as the UNSUBSCRIBE<br>packet. Even where no Topic Subscriptions are deleted, the Server MUST respond with<br>an UNSUBACK.|
|[MQTT-3.10.4-6]|If a Server receives an UNSUBSCRIBE packet that contains multiple Topic Filters, it<br>MUST process that packet as if it had received a sequence of multiple UNSUBSCRIBE<br>packets, except that it sends just one UNSUBACK response.|
|[MQTT-3.11.2-1]|The Server MUST NOT send this Property if it would increase the size of the<br>UNSUBACK packet beyond the Maximum Packet Size specified by the Client.|

|[MQTT-3.11.3-1]|The order of Reason Codes in the UNSUBACK packet MUST match the order of Topic<br>Filters in the UNSUBSCRIBE packet.|
|[MQTT-3.11.3-2]|The Server sending the UNSUBACK packet MUST use one of the UNSUBSCRIBE<br>Reason Code values for each Topic Filter received.|

|[MQTT-3.14.0-1]|A Server MUST NOT send a DISCONNECT until after it has sent a CONNACK with<br>Reason Code of less than 0x80.|
|[MQTT-3.14.1-1]|The Client or Server MUST validate that reserved bits are set to 0. If they are not zero it<br>sends a DISCONNECT packet with a Reason code of 0x81 (Malformed Packet).|

|[MQTT-4.1.0-1]|The Client and Server MUST NOT discard the Session State while the Network<br>Connection is open.|
|[MQTT-4.2.0-1]|A Client or Server MUST support the use of one or more underlying transport protocols<br>that provide an ordered, lossless, stream of bytes from the Client to Server and Server to<br>Client.|
|[MQTT-4.1.0-2]|The Server MUST discard the Session State when the Network Connection is closed and<br>the Session Expiry Interval has passed.|
|[MQTT-4.3.1-1]|In the QoS 0 delivery protocol, the sender MUST send a PUBLISH packet with QoS 0<br>and DUP flag set to 0.|
|[MQTT-4.3.2-1]|In the QoS 1 delivery protocol, the sender MUST assign an unused Packet Identifier each<br>time it has a new Application Message to publish.|

|[MQTT-4.3.2-2]|In the QoS 1 delivery protocol, the sender MUST send a PUBLISH packet containing this<br>Packet Identifier with QoS 1 and DUP flag set to 0.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-4.3.2-3]|In the QoS 1 delivery protocol, the sender MUST treat the PUBLISH packet as<br>“unacknowledged” until it has received the corresponding PUBACK packet from the<br>receiver.|
|[MQTT-4.3.2-4]|In the QoS 1 delivery protocol, the receiver MUST respond with a PUBACK packet<br>containing the Packet Identifier from the incoming PUBLISH packet, having accepted<br>ownership of the Application Message.|
|[MQTT-4.3.2-5]|In the QoS 1 delivery protocol, the receiver after it has sent a PUBACK packet the<br>receiver MUST treat any incoming PUBLISH packet that contains the same Packet<br>Identifier as being a new Application Message, irrespective of the setting of its DUP flag.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-1]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the sender MUST assign an unused Packet Identifier<br>when it has a new Application Message to publish.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-2]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the sender MUST send a PUBLISH packet containing this<br>Packet Identifier with QoS 2 and DUP flag set to 0.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-3]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the sender MUST treat the PUBLISH packet as<br>“unacknowledged” until it has received the corresponding PUBREC packet from the<br>receiver.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-4]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the sender MUST send a PUBREL packet when it<br>receives a PUBREC packet from the receiver with a Reason Code value less than 0x80.<br>This PUBREL packet MUST contain the same Packet Identifier as the original PUBLISH<br>packet.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-5]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the sender MUST treat the PUBREL packet as<br>“unacknowledged” until it has received the corresponding PUBCOMP packet from the<br>receiver.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-6]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the sender MUST NOT re-send the PUBLISH once it has<br>sent the corresponding PUBREL packet.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-7]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the sender MUST NOT apply Application Message expiry<br>if a PUBLISH packet has been sent.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-8]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the receiver MUST respond with a PUBREC containing<br>the Packet Identifier from the incoming PUBLISH packet, having accepted ownership of<br>the Application Message.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-9]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the receiver if it has sent a PUBREC with a Reason Code<br>of 0x80 or greater, the receiver MUST treat any subsequent PUBLISH packet that<br>contains that Packet Identifier as being a new Application Message.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-10]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the receiver until it has received the corresponding<br>PUBREL packet, the receiver MUST acknowledge any subsequent PUBLISH packet with<br>the same Packet Identifier by sending a PUBREC. It MUST NOT cause duplicate<br>messages to be delivered to any onward recipients in this case.|
|[MQTT-4.3.3-11]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the receiver MUST respond to a PUBREL packet by<br>sending a PUBCOMP packet containing the same Packet Identifier as the PUBREL.|

|[MQTT-4.3.3-12]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the receiver After it has sent a PUBCOMP, the receiver<br>MUST treat any subsequent PUBLISH packet that contains that Packet Identifier as<br>being a new Application Message.|

|[MQTT-4.3.3-13]|In the QoS 2 delivery protocol, the receiver MUST continue the QoS 2 acknowledgement<br>sequence even if it has applied Application Message expiry.|
|[MQTT-4.4.0-1]|When a Client reconnects with Clean Start set to 0 and a session is present, both the<br>Client and Server MUST resend any unacknowledged PUBLISH packets (where QoS ><br>0) and PUBREL packets using their original Packet Identifiers. This is the only<br>circumstance where a Client or Server is REQUIRED to resend messages. Clients and<br>Servers MUST NOT resend messages at any other time.|
|[MQTT-4.4.0-2]|If PUBACK or PUBREC is received containing a Reason Code of 0x80 or greater the<br>corresponding PUBLISH packet is treated as acknowledged, and MUST NOT be<br>retransmitted.|
|[MQTT-4.5.0-1]|When a Server takes ownership of an incoming Application Message it MUST add it to<br>the Session State for those Clients that have matching Subscriptions.|
|[MQTT-4.5.0-2]|The Client MUST acknowledge any Publish packet it receives according to the applicable<br>QoS rules regardless of whether it elects to process the Application Message that it<br>contains.|
|[MQTT-4.6.0-1]|When the Client re-sends any PUBLISH packets, it MUST re-send them in the order in<br>which the original PUBLISH packets were sent (this applies to QoS 1 and QoS 2<br>messages).|
|[MQTT-4.6.0-2]|The Client MUST send PUBACK packets in the order in which the corresponding<br>PUBLISH packets were received (QoS 1 messages).|
|[MQTT-4.6.0-3]|The Client MUST send PUBREC packets in the order in which the corresponding<br>PUBLISH packets were received (QoS 2 messages).|
|[MQTT-4.6.0-4]|The Client MUST send PUBREL packets in the order in which the corresponding<br>PUBREC packets were received (QoS 2 messages).|
|[MQTT-4.6.0-5]|When a Server processes a message that has been published to an Ordered Topic, it<br>MUST send PUBLISH packets to consumers (for the same Topic and QoS) in the order<br>that they were received from any given Client.|
|[MQTT-4.6.0-6]|A Server MUST treat every, Topic as an Ordered Topic when it is forwarding messages<br>on Non-shared Subscriptions.|
|[MQTT-4.7.0-1]|The wildcard characters can be used in Topic Filters, but MUST NOT be used within a<br>Topic Name.|
|[MQTT-4.7.1-1]|The multi-level wildcard character MUST be specified either on its own or following a<br>topic level separator. In either case it MUST be the last character specified in the Topic<br>Filter.|
|[MQTT-4.7.1-2]|The single-level wildcard can be used at any level in the Topic Filter, including first and<br>last levels. Where it is used, it MUST occupy an entire level of the filter.|
|[MQTT-4.7.2-1]|The Server MUST NOT match Topic Filters starting with a wildcard character (# or +) with<br>Topic Names beginning with a $ character.|



07 March 2019 Page 133 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-4.7.3-1]|All Topic Names and Topic Filters MUST be at least one character long.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-4.7.3-2]|Topic Names and Topic Filters MUST NOT include the null character (Unicode U+0000).|
|[MQTT-4.7.3-3]|Topic Names and Topic Filters are UTF-8 Encoded Strings; they MUST NOT encode to<br>more than 65,535 bytes.|
|[MQTT-4.7.3-4]|When it performs subscription matching the Server MUST NOT perform any<br>normalization of Topic Names or Topic Filters, or any modification or substitution of<br>unrecognized characters.|
|[MQTT-4.8.2-1]|A Shared Subscription's Topic Filter MUST start with $share/ and MUST contain a<br>ShareName that is at least one character long.|
|[MQTT-4.8.2-2]|The ShareName MUST NOT contain the characters "/", "+" or "#", but MUST be followed<br>by a "/" character. This "/" character MUST be followed by a Topic Filter.|
|[MQTT-4.8.2-3]|The Server MUST respect the granted QoS for the Clients subscription.|
|[MQTT-4.8.2-4]|The Server MUST complete the delivery of the message to that Client when it<br>reconnects.|
|[MQTT-4.8.2-5]|If the Clients Session terminates before the Client reconnects, the Server MUST NOT<br>send the Application Message to any other subscribed Client.|
|[MQTT-4.8.2-6]|If a Client responds with a PUBACK or PUBREC containing a Reason Code of 0x80 or<br>greater to a PUBLISH packet from the Server, the Server MUST discard the Application<br>Message and not attempt to send it to any other Subscriber.|
|[MQTT-4.9.0-1]|The Client or Server MUST set its initial send quota to a non-zero value not exceeding<br>the Receive Maximum.|
|[MQTT-4.9.0-2]|Each time the Client or Server sends a PUBLISH packet at QoS > 0, it decrements the<br>send quota. If the send quota reaches zero, the Client or Server MUST NOT send any<br>more PUBLISH packets with QoS > 0.|
|[MQTT-4.9.0-3]|The Client and Server MUST continue to process and respond to all other MQTT Control<br>Packets even if the quota is zero.|
|[MQTT-4.12.0-1]|If the Server does not support the Authentication Method supplied by the Client, it MAY<br>send a CONNACK with a Reason Code of 0x8C (Bad authentication method) or 0x87<br>(Not Authorized) as described in section 4.13 and MUST close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-4.12.0-2]|If the Server requires additional information to complete the authorization, it can send an<br>AUTH packet to the Client. This packet MUST contain a Reason Code of 0x18 (Continue<br>authentication).|
|[MQTT-4.12.0-3]|The Client responds to an AUTH packet from the Server by sending a further AUTH<br>packet. This packet MUST contain a Reason Code of 0x18 (Continue authentication).|
|[MQTT-4.12.0-4]|The Server can reject the authentication at any point in this process. It MAY send a<br>CONNACK with a Reason Code of 0x80 or above as described in section 4.13, and<br>MUST close the Network Connection.|



07 March 2019 Page 134 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

|[MQTT-4.12.0-5]|If the initial CONNECT packet included an Authentication Method property then all AUTH<br>packets, and any successful CONNACK packet MUST include an Authentication Method<br>Property with the same value as in the CONNECT packet.|
|---|---|
|[MQTT-4.12.0-6]|If the Client does not include an Authentication Method in the CONNECT, the Server<br>MUST NOT send an AUTH packet, and it MUST NOT send an Authentication Method in<br>the CONNACK packet.|
|[MQTT-4.12.0-7]|If the Client does not include an Authentication Method in the CONNECT, the Client<br>MUST NOT send an AUTH packet to the Server.|
|[MQTT-4.12.1-1]|If the Client supplied an Authentication Method in the CONNECT packet it can initiate a<br>re-authentication at any time after receiving a CONNACK. It does this by sending an<br>AUTH packet with a Reason Code of 0x19 (Re-authentication). The Client MUST set the<br>Authentication Method to the same value as the Authentication Method originally used to<br>authenticate the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-4.12.1-2]|If the re-authentication fails, the Client or Server SHOULD send DISCONNECT with an<br>appropriate Reason Code and MUST close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-4.13.1-1]|When a Server detects a Malformed Packet or Protocol Error, and a Reason Code is<br>given in the specification, it MUST close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-4.13.2-1]|The CONNACK and DISCONNECT packets allow a Reason Code of 0x80 or greater to<br>indicate that the Network Connection will be closed. If a Reason Code of 0x80 or greater<br>is specified, then the Network Connection MUST be closed whether or not the<br>CONNACK or DISCONNECT is sent.|
|[MQTT-6.0.0-1]|MQTT Control Packets MUST be sent in WebSocket binary data frames. If any other type<br>of data frame is received the recipient MUST close the Network Connection.|
|[MQTT-6.0.0-2]|A single WebSocket data frame can contain multiple or partial MQTT Control Packets.<br>The receiver MUST NOT assume that MQTT Control Packets are aligned on WebSocket<br>frame boundaries.|
|[MQTT-6.0.0-3]|The Client MUST include “mqtt” in the list of WebSocket Sub Protocols it offers.|
|[MQTT-6.0.0-4]|The WebSocket Subprotocol name selected and returned by the Server MUST be “mqtt”.|

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product

## 3907 **Appendix C. Summary of new features in MQTT v5.0** 3908 **(non-normative)** 

3909 The following new features are added to MQTT v5.0 

3910 

- 3911 • Session expiry 

- 3912 Split the Clean Session flag into a Clean Start flag which indicates that the session should start 3913 without using an existing session, and a Session Expiry interval which says how long to retain the 3914 session after a disconnect. The session expiry interval can be modified at disconnect. Setting of 3915 Clean Start to 1 and Session Expiry Interval to 0 is equivalent in MQTT v3.1.1 of setting Clean 3916 Session to 1. 

3917 

- 3918 • Message expiry 

- 3919 Allow an expiry interval to be set when a message is published. 

- 3920 

- 3921 • Reason code on all ACKs 3922 Change all response packets to contain a reason code. This include CONNACK, PUBACK, PUBREC, 3923 PUBREL, PUBCOMP, SUBACK, UNSUBACK, DISCONNECT, and AUTH. This allows the invoker to 3924 determine whether the requested function succeeded. 

- 3925 

- 3926 • Reason string on all ACKs 3927 Change most packets with a reason code to also allow an optional reason string. This is designed for 3928 problem determination and is not intended to be parsed by the receiver. 3929 

- 3930 • Server disconnect 

- 3931 Allow DISCONNECT to be sent by the Server to indicate the reason the connection is closed. 

- 3932 

- 3933 • Payload format and content type 3934 Allow the payload format (binary, text) and a MIME style content type to be specified when a 3935 message is published. These are forwarded on to the receiver of the message. 

- 3936 

- 3937 • Request / Response 

- 3938 Formalize the request/response pattern within MQTT and provide the Response Topic and 3939 Correlation Data properties to allow response messages to be routed back to the publisher of a 3940 request. Also, add the ability for the Client to get configuration information from the Server about how 3941 to construct the response topics. 

3942 

- 3943 • Shared Subscriptions 3944 Add shared subscription support allowing for load balanced consumers of a subscription 

3945 

- 3946 • Subscription ID 3947 Allow a numeric subscription identifier to be specified on a SUBSCRIBE, and returned on the 3948 message when it is delivered. This allows the Client to determine which subscription or subscriptions 3949 caused the message to be delivered. 

3950 

- 3951 • Topic Alias 3952 Decrease the size of the MQTT packet overhead by allowing the topic name to be abbreviated to a 3953 small integer. The Client and Server independently specify how many topic aliases they allow. 3954 

- 3955 • Flow control 3956 Allow the Client and Server to independently specify the number of outstanding reliable messages 3957 (QoS>0) they allow. The sender pauses sending such messages to stay below this quota. This is 3958 used to limit the rate of reliable messages, and to limit how many are in flight at one time. 

07 March 2019 Page 136 of 137 

mqtt-v5.0-os Standards Track Work Product 

Copyright © OASIS Open 2019. All Rights Reserved. 

- 3959 3960 • User properties 3961 Add User Properties to most packets. User properties on PUBLISH are included with the message 3962 and are defined by the Client applications. The user properties on PUBLISH and Will Properties are 3963 forwarded by the Server to the receiver of the message. User properties on the CONNECT, 3964 SUBSCRIBE, and UNSUBSCRIBE packets are defined by the Server implementation. The user 3965 properties on CONNACK PUBACK, PUBREC, PUBREL, PUBCOMP, SUBACK, UNSUBACK and 3966 AUTH packets are defined by the sender, and are unique to the sender implementation. The meaning 3967 of user properties is not defined by MQTT. 3968 

3969 • Maximum Packet Size 3970 Allow the Client and Server to independently specify the maximum packet size they support. It is an 3971 error for the session partner to send a larger packet. 3972 

- 3973 • Optional Server feature availability 3974 Define a set of features which the Server does not allow and provide a mechanism for the Server to 3975 specify this to the Client. The features which can be specified in this way are: Maximum QoS, Retain 3976 Available, Wildcard Subscription Available, Subscription Identifier Available, and Shared Subscription 3977 Available. It is an error for the Client to use features that the Server has declared are not available. 3978 

- 3979 It is possible in earlier versions of MQTT for a Server to not implement a feature by declaring that the 3980 Client is not authorized for that function. This feature allows such optional behavior to be declared 3981 and adds specific Reason Codes when the Client uses one of these features anyway. 

3982 

- 3983 • Enhanced authentication 

- 3984 Provide a mechanism to enable challenge/response style authentication including mutual 3985 authentication. This allows SASL style authentication to be used if supported by both Client and 3986 Server, and includes the ability for a Client to re-authenticate within a connection. 

3987 

- 3988 • Subscription options 3989 Provide subscription options primarily defined to allow for message bridge applications. These include 3990 an option to not send messages originating on this Client (noLocal), and options for handling retained 3991 messages on subscribe. 

3992 

- 3993 • Will delay 

- 3994 Add the ability to specify a delay between the end of the connection and sending the will message. 3995 This is designed so that if a connection to the session is re-established then the will message is not 3996 sent. This allows for brief interruptions of the connection without notification to others. 3997 

- 3998 • Server Keep Alive 3999 Allow the Server to specify the value it wishes the Client to use as a keep alive. This allows the 4000 Server to set a maximum allowed keepalive and still have the Client honor it. 4001 

- 4002 • Assigned ClientID 

- 4003 In cases where the ClientID is assigned by the Server, return the assigned ClientID. This also lifts the 4004 restriction that Server assigned ClientIDs can only be used with Clean Session=1 connections. 

- 4005 

- 4006 • Server reference 

- 4007 Allow the Server to specify an alternate Server to use on CONNACK or DISCONNECT. This can be 4008 used as a redirect or to do provisioning. 

- 4009
